```
I've been stuck in this room for some time now. They locked me in here and told
me the only way I can leave is if I solve their problem within five seconds. 
I've tried so much, but my algorithm keeps going over the time. Can you help me?

What I have to do is find the maximum contiguous sub-array within this array of 
numbers. They keep telling me my algorithm isn't efficient enough! If you can 
send me the indices of this array, I might live to see another day.

Format: "sum, i, j" Example: 103, 345, 455

sum = the maximum contiguous sum
i = start index of sub-array
j = end index of sub-array

Press Enter to get the arr
```

-15, 27, -79, 97, 54, 48, -27, 39, -21, 87, 75, 5, 33, -55, 50, 26, 52, 74, -38, -63, 26, -9, 41, -15, 3]

this array is different everytime netcat is run.

Also as soon as we press enter, a five second timer is set after which any response will be treated as wrong which makes copying the array into a program and pasting the output virtually impossible, which is why we use python sockets.

first off we define the function that will process the array, this will make use of the kadane algorithm to find the max sum sub-array. The code is as such:

```python
def maxSubArraySum(a,size):
 
    max_so_far = -maxsize - 1
    max_ending_here = 0
    start = 0
    end = 0
    s = 0
 
    for i in range(0,size):
 
        max_ending_here += a[i]
 
        if max_so_far < max_ending_here:
            max_so_far = max_ending_here
            start = s
            end = i
 
        if max_ending_here < 0:
            max_ending_here = 0
            s = i+1
 
    return str(max_so_far)+", "+ str(start)+", "+str(end)
```

this returns the required values in the defined format as a string.

Now to set up the socket and process the info:

```python
import socket
from sys import maxsize
from time import sleep

clientsocket = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)

clientsocket.connect(('chals3.umdctf.io', 6001))

data1 = clientsocket.recv(2048)
print(data1.decode())

res = "\n"
clientsocket.send(res.encode())

finalData=clientsocket.recv(20480).decode()
print(finalData)
```

This code establishes a connection with the server and prints the initial response and sends the enter command to the server and prints the response it gets. Since the array is very large it takes in 20 megabytes of data. This should've worked in theory but on printing the data displayed was incomplete. Output:


as you can see the entire array does not get read.

to overcome this, i use a loop to take packets of data and merge them into one string and use eval to convert into a list.

```python
finalData=""

for i in range(62):
    data = clientsocket.recv(20480).decode()
    finalData+=data
print(finalData)
obj = eval(finalData)
print(obj)
```

the loop runs 62 times and this number was found by trial and error.

now all thats left is to process this list and send the response to the server and print the output.

```python
result = maxSubArraySum(obj, len(obj))

dataFlag = clientsocket.recv(2048)
```

For Jay2 we follow the same steps but use a different algorithm which uses kadane in a listed method:

```python
def kadane(arr, start, finish, n):

    Sum = 0
    maxSum = -999999999999
    i = None
    finish[0] = -1
    local_start = 0
 
    for i in range(n):
        Sum += arr[i]
        if Sum < 0:
            Sum = 0
            local_start = i + 1
        elif Sum > maxSum:
            maxSum = Sum
            start[0] = local_start
            finish[0] = i
 
    if finish[0] != -1:
        return maxSum
 
    maxSum = arr[0]
    start[0] = finish[0] = 0
 
    for i in range(1, n):
        if arr[i] > maxSum:
            maxSum = arr[i]
            start[0] = finish[0] = i
    return maxSum

 
def findMaxSum(M):
    ROW=len(M)
    COL=len(M[0])
    maxSum, finalLeft = -999999999999, None
    finalRight, finalTop, finalBottom = None, None, None
    left, right, i = None, None, None
 
    temp = [None] * ROW
    Sum = 0
    start = [0]
    finish = [0]
 
    for left in range(COL):
        temp = [0] * ROW
        for right in range(left, COL):
            for i in range(ROW):
                temp[i] += M[i][right]
            Sum = kadane(temp, start, finish, ROW)

            if Sum > maxSum:
                maxSum = Sum
                finalLeft = left
                finalRight = right
                finalTop = start[0]
                finalBottom = finish[0]

    return str(maxSum)+", "+str(finalTop)+", "+str(finalBottom)+", "+str(finalLeft)+", "+str(finalRight)
```

the latter part of the code will be edited as follows:

```python
for i in range(279):
    data = clientsocket.recv(20480).decode()
    finalData+=data
obj = eval(finalData)
result = findMaxSum(obj)

clientsocket.send(result.encode())

dataFlag = clientsocket.recv(2048)
print (dataFlag.decode())
```

for this chal the array size was much larger hence the loop runs 279 times (found by trial and error)

output:

```
Oh YES! I'm free! Here, a token of my appreciation:
UMDCTF-{Pr0f3ss0r_Gr3n4nd3r}
```
